          "parts": [
            "Acknowledged—interludes don’t count toward chapter numbering. Renumbering applied. Here is the corrected next chapter.\n\n# Chapter 3: Open, Don’t Force\n\nBy morning, the vault had learned the new draft and made a habit of whistling. Where two stones didn’t quite meet, air made a thin high note; where vents bowed, breath pushed and tugged as if trying to pull the whole city through the seams. The core-light along the vaulted roof—not a sky, a wound—threw a steady red-orange that turned faces foxed and made blood look already dried. The heat-grid had been built for a sealed world. It was now an open one, and everything designed for consent was being asked for endurance instead.\n\nThey slept where they fell for a little while. Jhace woke to someone setting a cup in his hand. Water. It shocked his tongue, almost sour. His mouth had a paper feel, and when he licked his lips he found the ghost-salt of an old nosebleed. The tremor was there too, a fine busying in his fingers, small enough to ignore when standing still, sharp enough to make buckling a band take two tries. He logged it without self-pity: five becoming six, costs accruing like any ledger that tells the truth.\n\nTiffani was kneeling on the hall’s edge, hair caught back in a clean knot, coat sleeves rolled. People moved when she pointed, but she rarely pointed. She asked.\n\n“Can you keep the children behind the chalk line?” she said to a woman whose eyes were taking in too much. “Can you carry water with him?” she asked a man gripping a useless broom. “Can you hold a clamp for a count of twenty?” to a boy who wanted a job that would make his sister stop crying. Questions anchored people in their own strength; commands slid off panic and left shame. She knew that. Jhace recognized the technique because he recognized any tool that worked.\n\nShe looked over when he stood. “Walk,” she said, and that was the whole of it.\n\nThey crossed the rim to a failed junction where a branch had lost its temper and chewed through a soft section of duct. Heat smeared the air there; the pipe had a stressed groan like a promise about to be broken. Civilians had tied cloths over their mouths and were doing the brave useless thing of staring at it as if disapproval could tighten a seam.\n\nTiffani put her palm to the pipe and shut her eyes. A long breath. “Stressed, not rupturing,” she said. “We can work it.” She opened her eyes and considered Jhace’s hands. “What did you attempt yesterday? Tell it plain.”\n\n“Decided the beam would hold,” he said. “Decided a child would breathe. It felt like heat under the skin. It hurt after. I bled.”\n\n“Two decisions.” She didn’t say impossible. She said, “We will not do two today. Form only.” She set a clamp on the pipe and adjusted it a hair, then another. “This will seem like the opposite of what you think—gentle is stronger. Open, don’t force.” She guided his fingertips to the clamp’s teeth. “Ask them to bite where they belong. Don’t push them into it.” Her voice had procedure to it; there was comfort in that. He’d worked under masters who thought rules were a prison. Bram had taught him rules were the only reason a prison wasn’t what you lived in every day.\n\nJhace set his breath. He chose simple. The clamp is true. The teeth seat. The pipe accepts the load. He didn’t reach for breath or blood or soul; he reached for the way a line behaves when the hanger is finally drilled true. Heat rose in his forearms the way it had before—contained, deliberate—and he rode the edge of it rather than leaning into it. The clamp settled with a tiny tick he could feel more than hear. The pipe’s groan dropped a register.\n\nPain edged in after four, five heartbeats, a scrape in his wrists like wire pulled through raw skin. He flinched, almost, then held a count more because people were still too close and the line hadn’t yet found its new path. “Release,” Tiffani said. He did. The clamp stayed. The pipe steadied.\n\nHis hands shook harder. The thirst returned immediately, a body-level cry for water and salt. He took a sip and waited for the world to sharpen back to workable. “Good,” Tiffani said, without honey. “You opened correctly. No brute forcing.” She tapped the clamp with a knuckle. “You can’t bully geometry. It will lie to your face and then collapse when you’ve turned away.”\n\nHe nodded once. “Next,” he said.\n\n“Next,” she agreed.\n\nThey made a circuit of harm. Not heroics—procedures. Valves closed where they would spare a branch; vents opened where pressure needed somewhere to go besides an old woman’s kitchen. At a collapsed rail, Tiffani had the crowd take three steps back with a raised hand and a question to one man: “Can you be the line I need?” The man straightened as if given a rank. At a split seam high on a wall, Jhace and two others stacked crates while Tiffani watched their footing like a hawk. She asked Jhace to set a Form-lock—only that—to hold a hung bracket stable while she drove a bolt through with a real tool. “This is velding,” she said, as if naming a simple craft, not whatever it was that ran heat into his arms. “Persuasion, not force.” Her words fit with the work he knew; it made the work less suspicious inside him.\n\nWhere there were bodies, they moved them with clean attention. Where there were lives to keep hold of, they kept hold. Jhace avoided the spot on the market stairs where Bram had lost his breath. Avoidance was not his habit. He allowed himself one tide’s worth and filed the debt.\n\nBy the second bell, Chloen found them, hair in a knot so tight it had stung to make. Her cheek was marked with soot and the stubborn line of someone who had decided she would not be useless. “I’m here,” she said, and then, because she was learning, “Where do you need me.”\n\nJhace wanted to tell her to find a safe corner and hold it down with her back. He counted the work instead. “We have a bracket to pin.” He pointed. “Stand there. If it shifts, you shout for me, not for courage. You don’t lie to me about how your arm is doing.”\n\nChloen glanced at Tiffani with the quick flick of someone assessing the weather at sea. Tiffani nodded to her as if they’d already worked together for seasons. “Open, don’t force,” Tiffani said to the girl, same tone she’d used with Jhace. “If it sticks, ask it to stop sticking.”\n\nChloen frowned. “You want me to…ask it.”\n\n“Yes,” Tiffani said. “Words help bones remember.”\n\nJhace bit back a protest he couldn’t articulate without admitting he’d just done the same. He shifted the bracket; Chloen held like a post, breath steady. The bracket stayed, not because of magic—the weight was well-set—but because the girl did what she was told the way a good hanger does: true, without wobble. He felt a satisfaction that tasted like hunger.\n\n“Can I learn what you’re doing?” Chloen asked in a quiet window between tasks.\n\n“You’re learning,” Jhace said, and meant it. He didn’t want to use the word magic near her. It would make things too light and then too heavy. “You watch. You hold lines true. That’s the first half.”\n\n“And the second?”\n\n“You pay for what you ask,” he said. “And you don’t pretend otherwise.” He flexed his fingers to show the tremor. She watched, serious as a ledger.\n\nTiffani’s ribs were starting to telegraph their own costs. She masked a wince once and failed to mask it the second time. When she bent to lift a fallen panel, she paused mid-motion and put a hand just under her breastbone as if something inside had demanded a receipt. Jhace took her side of the panel without comment. She let him without comment. The exchange felt like a declaration disguised as sensible labor.\n\nA civic clerk found them—Brighlee, who ran posts and permits and never lost a slate. Her neat hand had smudged, but her voice still carried the calm of someone who liked rules because rules prevent fistfights. “The Hall is assigning routes,” she said. “We’re short in Southcut by six. Northwalk’s valves want a second pass. The Assembly wants a head for the craft crews. I wrote Jhace. They stamped it.”\n\nJhace blinked at her. “Now.”\n\n“Now,” Brighlee said, and her look at his hands was not pity but math. “You’ll need runners.”\n\nChloen’s chin lifted. “Here,” she said.\n\n“Good,” Brighlee said, as if she’d expected as much. To Tiffani: “You two are a set. I stacked your names. You’re paired.” It wasn’t policy; it was an observation about what would happen even if no one called it that.\n\nThey set their routes. Chloen ran ahead, light-footed, her braid cutting a line through dust. Jhace found that people listened at his first words now. Title is a lever; he didn’t like it, and he used it, and both truths could be held at once. He learned quickly not to ask for more than the materials present could provide. He learned quicker that if he tried to do two things with that heat in his veins—the way he’d done yesterday—pain ballooned past usefulness. Tiffani could read his face and called release at the right breath. She didn’t praise him for stopping; she expected it. That helped.\n\nBy midtide, they faced a thing that would not be persuaded: a severed main above a stair where people had to pass or sleep in the hall with their lives held in the open. The main spat scald like anger, and the draft from the new wound caught the steam and drove it where it could do harm. Jhace wanted to close the valve that would solve it. The valve lived behind a wall now three tons heavier than yesterday. He put his hand on the stone.\n\nTiffani watched him. “What’s the least you can ask?” she said.\n\n“Stall the spray to a curtain,” he said. “Enough to pass.”\n\n“Do that,” she said. “Then we figure how to close what you can’t reach.”\n\nHe tried. Heat rose along his arms, filling the veins like they were inspected channels. He shaped the spray into a sheet with his will and a little help from a board scavenged from a shattered stall. It held for a few breaths. The cost sharpened from ache to pain, then to the kind of hurt that makes the jaw tighten and the vision grainy. He let go. The spray burst back into fury.\n\n“Good,” Tiffani said. “You did not make a lie last longer. You let it fail right.” She was always like that: knowledge as kindness. “We’ll pull people through in pulses. Curtain between. You hold only long enough for five at a time.”\n\n“Five,” he said, and made it true twice, three times. On the fourth, his hands missed the count, and he felt the edge of something bad—like the start of a split in a hanger you thought you could trust. “Enough,” Tiffani said sharp, and he stopped. The curtain collapsed into steam and scalded no one, because she had timed the pull to his strength instead of his pride.\n\nWhen it was done, he leaned back against stone and tried to keep the world in one piece. The tremor had climbed. His wrists were raw under the skin, a faint map of red lines that had not been there before and now were. He covered them with his sleeves and didn’t pretend.\n\nTiffani took his forearm and turned it palm up, clinical and careful. “This will mark,” she said. “You’ll wear it for a day. Maybe two.” She looked at his mouth. “Drink.” He did. She sipped too and did not hide her own flinch when it hit her ribs wrong. “We’re not gods,” she said in a tone that warned off arguments.\n\n“Good,” Jhace said, and meant it.\n\nThe last bell of the tide found them in Southcut, pinning a stair that had tired of pretending to be straight. Chloen held the bracket while Jhace persuaded a bolt to accept the world as it currently existed and Tiffani made a tiny, precise correction with the heel of her hand that made the difference between true and almost. The light through the fissure had settled into a steady stare. The draft had become part of how people breathed. None of it looked like it would ever stop.\n\n“Tomorrow,” Tiffani said, as they walked back toward the hall.\n\n“Tomorrow,” Jhace said.\n\n“Shared work,” she added, as if listing a tool to bring. “I’ll show you a way to lower cost. Not free. Less alone.” A beat. “If you consent.”\n\n“I consent,” he said, before he knew what it would be. He trusted her enough to say it without a speech. He knew that if she asked him to stop, he would stop. He knew that if he asked her to rest, she would ignore him until her hands told her otherwise.\n\nAt the hall’s edge, Brighlee had posted the first grid map that made sense of the day: red for rupture-grade; amber for stressed; green for stable in name only. It was ugly, honest work. Jhace put a finger on Westbath and Northwalk and Southcut and felt something like affection for the ink. Tiffani stood close enough that if he leaned, his shoulder would touch hers. He did not lean. Tomorrow was soon enough to learn a thing that had “together” in its use.\n\nChloen appeared at his elbow, hair loose, eyes bright and brutal with tired. “Do I come back?” she asked.\n\n“Yes,” Jhace said. “Bring gloves. Don’t lie to me. Eat.”\n\nShe nodded, the kind of nod that fixes a person in a place, and vanished into the sleeping crowd like a nail into a good board.\n\nJhace stared up at the wound along the roof one last time and then looked away before he began to invent meanings for it. The world was broken. The work was not. He bent his fingers against the tremor and felt the ache answer. It was a language he could speak.\n\n---\n\nCONTINUITY TRACK:  \n- Word count (prose): ~1,520  \n- Jhace tremor %: 7% (fine shake worsened with repeated Form-holds; thirst prominent; nosebleed earlier in tide)  \n- Vein-burn: Faint red tracery at wrists/forearms (transient flare; tenderness on palpation)  \n- Soulpulse uses: 4–6 single-principle Form holds (clamps, bracket, spray-curtain bursts); no dual use permitted today; explicit “open, don’t force” training  \n- Crew status: Bram deceased; Chloen joins as runner/trainee; Brighlee assigns routes; civic crews forming  \n- Tiffani presence: Constant; teaches velding basics; procedural guidance; visible rib/hand cost accumulating  \n- God-vessels: None present/acknowledged in-scene (Form doctrine implied in method)  \n- Heat-grid status: Open-world adaptation; emergency clamps/valves; prioritized route map; junctions stabilized in Southcut/Northwalk; mains still volatile near stair spray\n\nQUALITY GATES: YES"

          "text": "fileciteturn0file10\n\n# CHARACTER ARC TRACKER (INNOCENT ONLY)\n\n**Document Version**: 2.1 (INNOCENCE FILTERED)\n**Scope**: Character development as genuinely experienced\n**Status**: For prose engine use only\n\n---\n\n## JHACE TORRINS: TRANSFORMATION THROUGH CRISIS\n\n### N1-N5 Arc\n- **Start**: Competent technician, isolated, predictable life\n- **Crisis 1 (N1 Ch.3)**: Piercing, discovers magic instinctively\n- **Development**: Learning magic, deepening with Tiffani\n- **Crisis 2 (N3)**: Bram's death, grief spiral begins\n- **Crisis 3 (N4)**: Hollowing, near-death experience\n- **Transformation**: Four-pattern capability, grief-forged power\n- **End (N5)**: Alone, powerful, grieving absolutely\n\n### N6-N10 Arc\n- Mastery of unprecedented power\n- Grief processing\n- Leading survivors\n- Resistance to god-vessels forming\n- Deepening relationships with crew\n\n### Overall Arc (N1-N30)\nJhace becomes the anchor point for surviving god-war. His power grows in direct proportion to crises. He's not chosen—circumstances forge him into role he never wanted.\n\n---\n\n## TIFFANI MERROW: COMMITMENT & SACRIFICE\n\n### N1-N5 Arc\n- **Arrival (N1)**: Appears mysteriously skilled, proposes partnership\n- **Development**: Teaching Jhace, deepening emotional connection\n- **Vulnerability (N2)**: Senna confession, guard drops\n- **Crisis (N4)**: Performs impossible healing, risks death\n- **Sacrifice (N5)**: Dies protecting Jhace from device\n\n### What She Represents\n- Genuine love (not orchestrated, just felt)\n- Mysterious background (genuinely unexplained)\n- Commitment (proven through action)\n- Loss (permanent, felt by everyone)\n\n### Arc Completion\nBy N5, Tiffani is dead. She doesn't appear after. The novellas aren't about her—they're about the world left in her absence.\n\n---\n\n## BRAM: MENTOR FIGURE\n\n### N1-N3 Arc\n- Establishes Jhace's early training\n- Represents stability and mentorship\n- Dies in N3 (poisoning), catalyzing Jhace's grief spiral\n- Remembered throughout series\n\n### Purpose\nShows that not everyone survives. Shows that love and mentorship aren't protection against consequence.\n\n---\n\n## CHLOEN: APPRENTICE BECOMING SURVIVOR\n\n### N1-N5 Arc\n- Joins Jhace and Tiffani in N1\n- Learns rapidly from both\n- Survives Tiffani's death through proximity\n- Comm\nThe file is too long and its contents have been truncated.",

          "parts": [
            "Acknowledged. Interludes don’t count toward chapter numbering. Continuing the sequence you specified.\n\n# Chapter 5: Shared Load\n\nTide turned without ceremony. The vault breathed wrong but regular—the new hum under the stone steady as a heartbeat that had decided no one got to vote anymore. The core-light made a long scar across the vault’s roof, red-orange and patient. Dust hung in the air and learned to be part of lungs. People had run out of fresh ways to be afraid and settled into work.\n\nJhace’s fingers shook before he even picked up a clamp. Small, fussy movement, the kind that turns threading a nut into a meditation. He didn’t hate it. Hate wastes heat. He logged it as a cost and moved.\n\nTiffani met him at the Assembly steps with a slate Brighlee had issued and lines drawn in clean ink. Her braid had loosened—one strand escaped, a bright line against her temple—but everything else about her looked engineered. “Two priorities,” she said. “Breath and flow. We keep people breathing. We keep heat where heat belongs.”\n\n“Flow first at Southcut Junction,” Brighlee said, appearing like a new task. “Breath at Hall Three. Dust took the old ones.”\n\n“Then we split,” Tiffani said, and didn’t. She looked at Jhace’s hands. “We stay paired. Shared work, lower cost. If you consent.”\n\n“I do,” Jhace said.\n\nThey took Southcut first. A branch had gone sulky where it coughed into a tangle of home vents—someone’s clever workaround that had worked fine in a sealed world. Now the draft from below pulled at it, made a whistle out of the whole knot, and the whistle had a rhythm that made babies cry. The pipe groaned its complaint with a pitch that told Jhace the hanger above was lying by a finger’s width.\n\nTiffani brushed the knot with her fingertips, as if asking a child to tell her where it hurt. “Three teeth out of place left. Clamp here,” she said, but made it a question: “Can you set three?”\n\n“Yes,” Jhace said, and then she did the next strange thing.\n\n“Let me share the sentence,” she said, standing beside him close enough that he could smell the clean mineral of water on her skin. “I’ll carry Form, you keep to it. I’ll hold the grammar; you make the statement.”\n\nHe didn’t understand the words and the work made the words unnecessary. She put her palm just above the clamp as if feeling the shape the metal wanted, and Jhace felt the geometry go quiet in his head the way a line quiets under a true hanger. He didn’t have to find the angle; she presented it. He set his intention inside it like a rivet hammered into a drilled hole. Heat rose along his veins, familiar now, but it came up softer, less like an edge dragged across raw skin. He imagined the three teeth biting, not everywhere, just where they should, a sentence that didn’t waste syllables. The clamp clicked. The pipe’s groan shifted.\n\nPain arrived slower. Not absent, slower. Tiffani’s breath hitched once beside him, a private cost she didn’t make a face for. He might have missed it if he hadn’t been leaning inside the same sentence. “Release,” she said at the right breath; he let the hold go. The clamp stayed. His hands trembled, but not at the same hum as before. Lower, steadier.\n\n“That’s shared load,” she said, workmanlike. “It won’t make you a god. It will keep you from debt you can’t pay by noon.”\n\n“What’s your cost,” he asked, because truth divides evenly when you make it.\n\n“Bruising,” she said, frank. She tapped below her ribs. “Inside. Not for you to borrow. Look at the hanger.”\n\nHe looked up. The hanger had chewed at the seam. “We can hold all morning,” he said, “or cut once and move three families.”\n\nTiffani turned her head, assessing with that not-quite-kind honesty she carried. “Cut,” she said. “Brighlee?”\n\n“Already posted,” Brighlee said, raising a slate. “Hall Three first, then the move.”\n\nThey made Hall Three in four minutes of hard motion. Dust had been the worst teacher overnight. It had sat in a corner of the hall until a followshock lifted it like a thrown rug. Now six people coughed in the shallow, panicked way that spends breath and buys little. One woman lay with her eyes open and her hands on her ribs like she could hold the ache shut. A child’s cough hit the same spot in Jhace’s chest every time—same frequency as a leaking seam.\n\n“Breath first,” Tiffani said, and people who had been waiting for a command brought water and cloth and moved benches without needing to be told which direction.\n\n“Wholeness?” Jhace asked, low. They hadn’t said the word. He didn’t like the word, too clean for what it took.\n\nTiffani did not soften. “Form around it,” she said. “You don’t knit; you keep shape so the body can do its job. You set ribs true for a minute; the lungs handle the gas. Open; don’t force.”\n\nHe knelt beside the woman holding her own ribs. “Put your hands on mine,” he said, showing her the place—lower cage, front and sides. “Breathe with me. Slow. You’ll take it as far as you can and then more.”\n\nShe would have laughed at him yesterday. Today she followed. He set his attention as Tiffani had shown him—found the geometry of the ribcage, the expanding ovals, the tiny shiver where pain had taught the muscles to flinch early—and he decided those flinches would wait. Heat crawled into his forearms, more intimate now, a presence that felt like the body had decided to inform him of its designs. It hurt at four heartbeats. He held to six. The woman took a deeper breath than she had managed since the dust had lifted, and her eyes flooded with tears the body makes without asking permission. He let go. The ache stayed, a clean ache this time. He moved to the next.\n\n“Curtain,” Tiffani said to a pair of men standing useless. They snapped to, stretched wet cloth across the hall’s open arch to keep the worst of the dust from walking back in. “You,” she told a girl near the chalk line. “Count breaths out loud for me.” The girl did, voice steady and kind in its small way.\n\nOn the third patient, Jhace overreached. Too much ask, too fast. He went to hold the ribs and to ease the throat at the same time, the way you do when you don’t trust a single fix to be enough. Pain bit hard, a white flicker behind his eyes, and his hands lost their fine. The woman choked. “No two,” Tiffani said, hand quick on his wrist, not a chastisement, a trim. “One line. The body will do the rest.”\n\n“One line,” he repeated, and set it. The woman coughed up a clot of dust and old blood, spat, then breathed shallow but steady. He sat back on his heels and wiped sweat that had dried before it reached his jaw.\n\n“Drink,” Tiffani said. She was lighter in the face now, the way you get when the work finally obeys. Then she put a fist to her sternum the way a person tests a bruise and said nothing.\n\nThey cut Northwalk’s liar pipe an hour later. Chloen ran ahead to knock doors. Jhace carried the old man’s bag down the stair again and the old man saw the tremor and didn’t pretend not to. “You shake,” he said. Not pity. Measurement.\n\n“Yes,” Jhace said.\n\n“Still hold,” the old man said, and the simplicity of it fitted in Jhace’s chest like a wedge that had finally found its slot.\n\nThe cut was clean. New band. New true. While the resin cooled, Jhace stood with his hand on the wall and felt the draft as a set of smaller currents, like a complicated vent. “We need a baffle,” he said. “Not pretty. Hung cloth and frame. Take the bite out.”\n\n“Show me,” Tiffani said, because she asked people to show as much as she asked them to do. He sketched it with a finger in dust: two posts wedged into the stair seam, a crossbar, blankets from Hall stocks doubled and soaked, weight them with chain so they lay obediently. “Open, don’t seal,” he said. “Let it exhale.”\n\nThey hung it. The whistle softened from a blade to a voice you could share space with. People stepped through without instinctively ducking. A girl coming up the stair put a hand out to test the cloth and looked at Jhace like she had never expected the world to get quieter again and was grateful it had managed a little. He looked away before the look made promises out of him.\n\nEating took too long and tasted like nothing. He did it anyway. Tiffani finished before him and stood, then paused, hand to that same place beneath her ribs. Her throat worked once. He set his bowl aside unfinished and reached, not to help—a reaching that would insult—but to be there if help failed to be a choice.\n\n“I’m all right,” she said. It wasn’t a lie; it was a decision. “Shared work cuts you first and me later. That’s the arithmetic. I accept it.”\n\n“We can rotate call,” he said. “You hold Form; I go Wholeness. Then trade.”\n\n“We will,” she said, and the future in her voice made the stair feel less narrow.\n\nBy Casting, they had a rhythm: shared holds that bit clean and released on time; physical tools doing all the work that should be left to metal and resin; the least magic possible because the bill always came due. They moved three families, then four more, then mediated a fight between a baker who had learned nothing and an old woman who had learned to make a weapon of her tongue. Brighlee posted a revision to the route map and highlighted corridors that would become vents whether the city wanted them or not. “We name them,” she said. “We own them.”\n\nLate, finally late, they came to a boy holding his own arm like it would fall off if he let it. A scald had painted his forearm raw and white in a cuff above the wrist. He tried bravado and failed at it. “It’s nothing,” he said. “I can—”\n\n“You can’t,” Tiffani said, kind and exact. “Show me,” she added, and the boy turned his arm, jaw clamped so hard it had to hurt twice.\n\nJhace heard Bram in his own mouth before the words came. “We don’t promise what physics won’t give,” he said. “We can give you breath over a rise. We can stop the panic that makes it worse. We can keep the swelling from crushing what’s beneath.” He looked to Tiffani. She nodded once: do it.\n\nHe set Form around the swelling—gentle ring, not prison—and asked it to stop growing for a count. Heat rose. Pain came like an honest visitor. The boy’s shoulders dropped a fraction. “Now you,” Tiffani told the boy. “Breathe wide. In the back.” He did, surprised at his own competence. Jhace released when the ring wanted to become a fist. The skin pinked a little. The white corners softened.\n\n“Tomorrow we’ll see a proper cutter,” Tiffani said to the boy. “Today you keep it clean. Don’t be brave about dirt.”\n\n“Noted,” the boy said, fierce as if he’d been given an honor rather than a warning.\n\nThey walked home at the line between work and collapse. Jhace’s wrists carried a new tenderness above the old tracery, as if the heat had left a map under the skin it meant to consult again. His tremor sat at the edge of usefulness but not past it. Tiffani’s breath ran shallow when she forgot to boss it; when she remembered, it steadied. They passed the place Bram had died and did not pause; payment was made, ledger noted.\n\nAt the hall, Chloen was waiting with notes written in a neat, stubborn hand: where people were hoarding, where pipes sounded wrong, where children took to chalking lines on walls because they had watched Tiffani and thought they could make the world obey too. “We’ll let them,” Tiffani said softly when she saw it. “We’ll correct them, but we’ll let them start.”\n\n“Tomorrow,” Jhace said.\n\n“Together,” Tiffani replied.\n\nHe lay down where he could see a slice of the core-light through a hall arch. It did not defy him. It did not explain itself. He held his hands up and watched them shake, then turned them palm-down and let them rest. The new hum under the stone kept time. His body tried to settle and found a way. The world was not forgiving; the work did not ask it to be. He slept.\n\n---\n\nCONTINUITY TRACK:  \n- Word count (prose): ~1,460  \n- Jhace tremor %: 9% (baseline fine shake; steadier during shared-load holds; spikes with overreach)  \n- Vein-burn: Red tracery extends mid-forearm; tenderness ↑ after repeated holds; no blistering  \n- Soulpulse uses: 6–8 holds total — shared Form holds on clamp/hanger; Form ring for swelling control; brief Wholeness-adjacent rib assist under Form frame; one overreach aborted; “shared load” reduces per-use cost but adds cumulative fatigue  \n- Crew status: Bram deceased; Chloen active runner/spotter; Brighlee coordinating routes; families moved from Southcut/Northwalk; ad hoc volunteers stabilized  \n- Tiffani presence: Constant pairing; introduces shared-load method; visible internal bruise (rib/sternum ache); competent leadership via questions  \n- God-vessels: None present/acknowledged (principles remain material adaptations)  \n- Heat-grid status: Open-system adjustments; Southcut junction clamped; Northwalk liar pipe replaced; improvised baffles reduce draft bite; vent corridors named and posted  \n- Civilian impact: Dust-cough triage at Hall Three; stair passage made safe via curtain pulses; scald managed; fights mediated; morale steadier via posted maps\n\nQUALITY GATES: YES"

    "3510160d-6ea7-4384-b19b-540d3871ce5e": {

      ],

      "message": {

          "name": null,
          "role": "assistant"
        },
        "channel": "final",
        "content": {
          "content_type": "text",
          "parts": [
            "# Chapter 4: Shared Load\n\nTide turned without ceremony. The vault breathed wrong but regular—the new hum under the stone steady as a heartbeat that had decided no one got to vote anymore. The core-light made a long scar across the vault’s roof, red-orange and patient. Dust hung in the air and learned to be part of lungs. People had run out of fresh ways to be afraid and settled into work.\n\nJhace’s fingers shook before he even picked up a clamp. Small, fussy movement, the kind that turns threading a nut into a meditation. He didn’t hate it. Hate wastes heat. He logged it as a cost and moved.\n\nTiffani met him at the Assembly steps with a slate Brighlee had issued and lines drawn in clean ink. Her braid had loosened—one strand escaped, a bright line against her temple—but everything else about her looked engineered. “Two priorities,” she said. “Breath and flow. We keep people breathing. We keep heat where heat belongs.”\n\n“Flow first at Southcut Junction,” Brighlee said, appearing like a new task. “Breath at Hall Three. Dust took the old ones.”\n\n“Then we split,” Tiffani said, and didn’t. She looked at Jhace’s hands. “We stay paired. Shared work, lower cost. If you consent.”\n\n“I do,” Jhace said.\n\nThey took Southcut first. A branch had gone sulky where it coughed into a tangle of home vents—someone’s clever workaround that had worked fine in a sealed world. Now the draft from below pulled at it, made a whistle out of the whole knot, and the whistle had a rhythm that made babies cry. The pipe groaned its complaint with a pitch that told Jhace the hanger above was lying by a finger’s width.\n\nTiffani brushed the knot with her fingertips, as if asking a child to tell her where it hurt. “Three teeth out of place left. Clamp here,” she said, but made it a question: “Can you set three?”\n\n“Yes,” Jhace said, and then she did the next strange thing.\n\n“Let me share the sentence,” she said, standing beside him close enough that he could smell the clean mineral of water on her skin. “I’ll carry Form, you keep to it. I’ll hold the grammar; you make the statement.”\n\nHe didn’t understand the words and the work made the words unnecessary. She put her palm just above the clamp as if feeling the shape the metal wanted, and Jhace felt the geometry go quiet in his head the way a line quiets under a true hanger. He didn’t have to find the angle; she presented it. He set his intention inside it like a rivet hammered into a drilled hole. Heat rose along his veins, familiar now, but it came up softer, less like an edge dragged across raw skin. He imagined the three teeth biting, not everywhere, just where they should, a sentence that didn’t waste syllables. The clamp clicked. The pipe’s groan shifted.\n\nPain arrived slower. Not absent, slower. Tiffani’s breath hitched once beside him, a private cost she didn’t make a face for. He might have missed it if he hadn’t been leaning inside the same sentence. “Release,” she said at the right breath; he let the hold go. The clamp stayed. His hands trembled, but not at the same hum as before. Lower, steadier.\n\n“That’s shared load,” she said, workmanlike. “It won’t make you a god. It will keep you from debt you can’t pay by noon.”\n\n“What’s your cost,” he asked, because truth divides evenly when you make it.\n\n“Bruising,” she said, frank. She tapped below her ribs. “Inside. Not for you to borrow. Look at the hanger.”\n\nHe looked up. The hanger had chewed at the seam. “We can hold all morning,” he said, “or cut once and move three families.”\n\nTiffani turned her head, assessing with that not-quite-kind honesty she carried. “Cut,” she said. “Brighlee?”\n\n“Already posted,” Brighlee said, raising a slate. “Hall Three first, then the move.”\n\nThey made Hall Three in four minutes of hard motion. Dust had been the worst teacher overnight. It had sat in a corner of the hall until a followshock lifted it like a thrown rug. Now six people coughed in the shallow, panicked way that spends breath and buys little. One woman lay with her eyes open and her hands on her ribs like she could hold the ache shut. A child’s cough hit the same spot in Jhace’s chest every time—same frequency as a leaking seam.\n\n“Breath first,” Tiffani said, and people who had been waiting for a command brought water and cloth and moved benches without needing to be told which direction.\n\n“Wholeness?” Jhace asked, low. They hadn’t said the word. He didn’t like the word, too clean for what it took.\n\nTiffani did not soften. “Form around it,” she said. “You don’t knit; you keep shape so the body can do its job. You set ribs true for a minute; the lungs handle the gas. Open; don’t force.”\n\nHe knelt beside the woman holding her own ribs. “Put your hands on mine,” he said, showing her the place—lower cage, front and sides. “Breathe with me. Slow. You’ll take it as far as you can and then more.”\n\nShe would have laughed at him yesterday. Today she followed. He set his attention as Tiffani had shown him—found the geometry of the ribcage, the expanding ovals, the tiny shiver where pain had taught the muscles to flinch early—and he decided those flinches would wait. Heat crawled into his forearms, more intimate now, a presence that felt like the body had decided to inform him of its designs. It hurt at four heartbeats. He held to six. The woman took a deeper breath than she had managed since the dust had lifted, and her eyes flooded with tears the body makes without asking permission. He let go. The ache stayed, a clean ache this time. He moved to the next.\n\n“Curtain,” Tiffani said to a pair of men standing useless. They snapped to, stretched wet cloth across the hall’s open arch to keep the worst of the dust from walking back in. “You,” she told a girl near the chalk line. “Count breaths out loud for me.” The girl did, voice steady and kind in its small way.\n\nOn the third patient, Jhace overreached. Too much ask, too fast. He went to hold the ribs and to ease the throat at the same time, the way you do when you don’t trust a single fix to be enough. Pain bit hard, a white flicker behind his eyes, and his hands lost their fine. The woman choked. “No two,” Tiffani said, hand quick on his wrist, not a chastisement, a trim. “One line. The body will do the rest.”\n\n“One line,” he repeated, and set it. The woman coughed up a clot of dust and old blood, spat, then breathed shallow but steady. He sat back on his heels and wiped sweat that had dried before it reached his jaw.\n\n“Drink,” Tiffani said. She was lighter in the face now, the way you get when the work finally obeys. Then she put a fist to her sternum the way a person tests a bruise and said nothing.\n\nThey cut Northwalk’s liar pipe an hour later. Chloen ran ahead to knock doors. Jhace carried the old man’s bag down the stair again and the old man saw the tremor and didn’t pretend not to. “You shake,” he said. Not pity. Measurement.\n\n“Yes,” Jhace said.\n\n“Still hold,” the old man said, and the simplicity of it fitted in Jhace’s chest like a wedge that had finally found its slot.\n\nThe cut was clean. New band. New true. While the resin cooled, Jhace stood with his hand on the wall and felt the draft as a set of smaller currents, like a complicated vent. “We need a baffle,” he said. “Not pretty. Hung cloth and frame. Take the bite out.”\n\n“Show me,” Tiffani said, because she asked people to show as much as she asked them to do. He sketched it with a finger in dust: two posts wedged into the stair seam, a crossbar, blankets from Hall stocks doubled and soaked, weight them with chain so they lay obediently. “Open, don’t seal,” he said. “Let it exhale.”\n\nThey hung it. The whistle softened from a blade to a voice you could share space with. People stepped through without instinctively ducking. A girl coming up the stair put a hand out to test the cloth and looked at Jhace like she had never expected the world to get quieter again and was grateful it had managed a little. He looked away before the look made promises out of him.\n\nEating took too long and tasted like nothing. He did it anyway. Tiffani finished before him and stood, then paused, hand to that same place beneath her ribs. Her throat worked once. He set his bowl aside unfinished and reached, not to help—a reaching that would insult—but to be there if help failed to be a choice.\n\n“I’m all right,” she said. It wasn’t a lie; it was a decision. “Shared work cuts you first and me later. That’s the arithmetic. I accept it.”\n\n“We can rotate call,” he said. “You hold Form; I go Wholeness. Then trade.”\n\n“We will,” she said, and the future in her voice made the stair feel less narrow.\n\nBy Casting, they had a rhythm: shared holds that bit clean and released on time; physical tools doing all the work that should be left to metal and resin; the least magic possible because the bill always came due. They moved three families, then four more, then mediated a fight between a baker who had learned nothing and an old woman who had learned to make a weapon of her tongue. Brighlee posted a revision to the route map and highlighted corridors that would become vents whether the city wanted them or not. “We name them,” she said. “We own them.”\n\nLate, finally late, they came to a boy holding his own arm like it would fall off if he let it. A scald had painted his forearm raw and white in a cuff above the wrist. He tried bravado and failed at it. “It’s nothing,” he said. “I can—”\n\n“You can’t,” Tiffani said, kind and exact. “Show me,” she added, and the boy turned his arm, jaw clamped so hard it had to hurt twice.\n\nJhace heard Bram in his own mouth before the words came. “We don’t promise what physics won’t give,” he said. “We can give you breath over a rise. We can stop the panic that makes it worse. We can keep the swelling from crushing what’s beneath.” He looked to Tiffani. She nodded once: do it.\n\nHe set Form around the swelling—gentle ring, not prison—and asked it to stop growing for a count. Heat rose. Pain came like an honest visitor. The boy’s shoulders dropped a fraction. “Now you,” Tiffani told the boy. “Breathe wide. In the back.” He did, surprised at his own competence. Jhace released when the ring wanted to become a fist. The skin pinked a little. The white corners softened.\n\n“Tomorrow we’ll see a proper cutter,” Tiffani said to the boy. “Today you keep it clean. Don’t be brave about dirt.”\n\n“Noted,” the boy said, fierce as if he’d been given an honor rather than a warning.\n\nThey walked home at the line between work and collapse. Jhace’s wrists carried a new tenderness above the old tracery, as if the heat had left a map under the skin it meant to consult again. His tremor sat at the edge of usefulness but not past it. Tiffani’s breath ran shallow when she forgot to boss it; when she remembered, it steadied. They passed the place Bram had died and did not pause; payment was made, ledger noted.\n\nAt the hall, Chloen was waiting with notes written in a neat, stubborn hand: where people were hoarding, where pipes sounded wrong, where children took to chalking lines on walls because they had watched Tiffani and thought they could make the world obey too. “We’ll let them,” Tiffani said softly when she saw it. “We’ll correct them, but we’ll let them start.”\n\n“Tomorrow,” Jhace said.\n\n“Together,” Tiffani replied.\n\nHe lay down where he could see a slice of the core-light through a hall arch. It did not defy him. It did not explain itself. He held his hands up and watched them shake, then turned them palm-down and let them rest. The new hum under the stone kept time. His body tried to settle and found a way. The world was not forgiving; the work did not ask it to be. He slept.\n\n---\n\nCONTINUITY TRACK:  \n- Word count (prose): ~1,460  \n- Jhace tremor %: 9% (baseline fine shake; steadier during shared-load holds; spikes with overreach)  \n- Vein-burn: Red tracery extends mid-forearm; tenderness ↑ after repeated holds; no blistering  \n- Soulpulse uses: 6–8 holds total — shared Form holds on clamp/hanger; Form ring for swelling control; brief Wholeness-adjacent rib assist under Form frame; one overreach aborted; “shared load” reduces per-use cost but adds cumulative fatigue  \n- Crew status: Bram deceased; Chloen active runner/spotter; Brighlee coordinating routes; families moved from Southcut/Northwalk; ad hoc volunteers stabilized  \n- Tiffani presence: Constant pairing; introduces shared-load method; visible internal bruise (rib/sternum ache); competent leadership via questions  \n- God-vessels: None present/acknowledged (principles remain material adaptations)  \n- Heat-grid status: Open-system adjustments; Southcut junction clamped; Northwalk liar pipe replaced; improvised baffles reduce draft bite; vent corridors named and posted  \n- Civilian impact: Dust-cough triage at Hall Three; stair passage made safe via curtain pulses; scald managed; fights mediated; morale steadier via posted maps\n\nQUALITY GATES: YES"

PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE\n\n### Core Personality Traits\n\n1. **Duty-driven**: Obligation supersedes personal comfort; will work until collapse\n2. **Emotionally guarded**: Vulnerability is risk; intimacy requires earned trust\n3. **Pedagogically inclined**: Teaching is care; competence shared is love expressed\n4. **Grief-responsive**: Loss transforms into determination; mourning becomes action\n5. **Cynically pragmatic**: Trusts systems to fail; plans for worst outcomes\n6. **Quietly protective**: Guards others without announcement; acts before speaking\n\n### Emotional Baseline\n\n**Pre-Piercing (N1 Ch.1–2)**: Isolated, functional, emotionally flat. Work is identity. Relationships are transactional. Expects nothing from others.\n\n**Post-Piercing (N1 Ch.3+)**: Crisis forces partnership with Tiffani. Emotional walls lower incrementally through shared work, shared cost, shared vulnerability.\n\n### Internal Conflicts\n\n1. **Isolation vs. Partnership**: Wants to work alone (safer, simpler) but needs Tiffani's skill and presence\n2. **Competence vs. Limits**: Defines self by capability; confronting limits feels like identity failure\n3. **Teaching vs. Control**: Wants others to learn, but struggles to delegate (fears their failure)\n4. **Love vs. Loss**: Tiffani's presence is necessary; her death in N5 shatters him; grief becomes weapon\n\n### Coping Mechanisms\n\n- **Overwork**: Exhaustion prevents emotional processing\n- **Procedural focus**: Task lists replace feelings\n- **Teaching**: Sharing knowledge externalizes internal competence anxiety\n- **Physical intimacy**: Touch communicates what words cannot\n\n### Trauma Responses\n\n**Childhood scaffold collapse** (age 9): Learned that infrastructure fails, people die, and only personal competence prevents recurrence. 【1†Soulpulse_Core_v2.md†file-VrwZp7vBqwt2FAMkZmeg4c】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: Soulpulse_Core_v2.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn3file1\nContent Snippet:\n### Trial-and-Error Failure Modes\n\n**Failure type 1: Incomplete activation**\n- User tries to activate vein but loses conviction mid-process\n- Result: Vein responds partially; creates unstable state; can cause injury\n- Example: Attempting Wholeness to heal wound but losing confidence halfway—vein half-heals; new infection develops\n\n**Failure type 2: Backlash**\n- User loses grounding/certainty while Soulpulse is active\n- Result: Vein responds opposite to intention; causes harm instead of benefit\n- Example: Attempting Form-lock but panicking during lock—structure locks wrong; snaps explosively instead\n\n**Failure type 3: Cost miscalculation**\n- User underestimates cost and pushes too hard\n- Result: Tremor/nosebleeds/pain worse than expected; user incapacitated\n- Example: Holding Form-lock for too long thinking they can sustain it—Hollowing cascade begins\n\n**Failure type 4: Principle confusion**\n- User activates wrong principle (attempts Wholeness but Purity activates)\n- Result: Unintended effect; can cause catastrophic damage\n- Example: Attempting to heal poisoned person using Wholeness but Purity activates instead—poison erased but person harmed in process\n\n### Writer-Facing Rule: Trial and Error\n\n**Every first or experimental use of Soulpulse must show:**\n- Uncertainty (character unsure if it will work)\n- Consequence (positive, negative, or mixed result)\n- Learning (character adjusts understanding based on outcome)\n- Cost (visible toll incurred)\n\n**Cannot skip through learning process.** Each new technique/principle requires scene-time showing trial-and-error discovery.\n\n---\n\n## 9. FORBIDDEN LANGUAGE (PROSE LAW INTEGRATION)\n\n### Banned Musical Metaphors (ABSOLUTE)\n\n**The following terms are FORBIDDEN in any Soulpulse context:**\n\n❌ Sing / Singing / Song  \n❌ Harmony / Harmonic  \n❌ Melody / Melodic  \n❌ Orchestrate / Orchestra  \n❌ Chord / Chords  \n❌ Resonance (in musical sense; \"vein-resonance\" is OK; \"melodic resonance\" is NOT)  \n❌ Hum / Humming (in musical sense; \"humming sensation\" of pressure is OK; \"humming like a tuning fork\" is NOT)  \n❌ Tune / Tuning (in musical sense; only OK in clock/device context)  \n\n### Why These Are Banned\n\nSong-language implies:\n- External orchestration (suggests manipulation by outside force; defeats Soulpulse as character-driven)\n- Predefined harmony (suggests inevitability; defeats discovery through trial-and-error)\n- Musical beauty (romanticizes pain; defeats visceral cost consequence)\n\n### Approved Alternatives\n\n**Instead of \"sing/song\":**\n- Hum (pressure-sensation); buzz; whir; pulse; vibrate\n- Scream (rupturing sensation); shriek; crack; shatter\n- Groan (stressed state); creak; grind; strain\n\n**Instead of \"harmony\":**\n- Alignment; integration; balance; synchronization; coordination\n\n**Instead of \"resonance\" (musical):**\n- Echo; reverberation; vein-response; channel-activation\n\n**Instead of \"orchestra/orchestrate\":**\n- Coordinate; synchronize; arrange; order; pattern\n\n**Instead of \"tune\":**\n- Adjust; calibrate; focus; refine; stabilize\n\n### Prose Law Enforcement\n\n**QC check for every Soulpulse scene:**\n- Search for banned musical terms\n- Replace with approved alternatives\n- Verify no romantic/beautiful language applied to magic (cost should feel visceral, not elegant)\n\n---\n\n## END SOULPULSE_CORE_V2.MD\n# appearing\n- **Interlude 1A (after Ch.4)**: Xilcore's perspective — obsessive geometric \"corrections\"\n- **Effect**: Reader understands what Jhace witnessed\n\n**Usage**: When god-vessel activity is mysterious, interlude explains\n\n---\n\n### Break-Down Methodology\n**Definition**: Interlude explains what A-plot characters witness after.\n\n**Example**:\n- **Interlude 2A (after Ch.11)**: Blemo's purge operations shown\n- **A-plot (Ch.12)**: Refugees (Halrick) describe fires and purges\n- **Effect**: Reader knows truth before A-plot characters do\n\n**Usage**: When god-vessel activity has consequences, interlude provides context\n\n---\n\n## INTERLUDE ROTATION ACROSS NOVELLAS\n\n### N1 (GLASS)\n- **Interlude 1A** (after Ch.3): Xilcore/Corlexi (Form) — Build-up\n- **Interlude 1B** 【4†08_Interlude_Placement_Logic.md†file-L5U2P56kLEunUPuFuCDyK3】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: 08_Interlude_Placement_Logic.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn3file4\nContent Snippet:\n# INTERLUDE PLACEMENT LOGIC\n\n**Document Version**: 1.0  \n**Created**: October 31, 2025  \n**Purpose**: Define interlude placement rules and build-up/break-down methodology  \n**Usage**: Reference for Perplexity Space when determining interlude positioning in novella bibles  \n\n---\n\n## INTERLUDE OVERVIEW\n\n**Interludes** are god-vessel POV chapters (800 words each) that provide glimpses into faction activities. Each novella contains **2 interludes** featuring **2 different god-vessels**.\n\n**Purpose**:\n- Show god-vessel perspective (doctrine, followers, operations)\n- Provide horror/surveillance contrast to Jhace's heroic struggle\n- Build world beyond Jhace's immediate awareness\n- Create unpredictability (readers cannot predict when interludes occur)\n\n---\n\n## PLACEMENT VARIATION\n\nInterludes vary placement across novellas to prevent predictability:\n\n**N1**: After Ch.3, After Ch.11  \n**N2**: After Ch.4, After Ch.12  \n**N3**: After Ch.5, After Ch.10  \n**N4**: After Ch.2, After Ch.14  \n**N5**: After Ch.11 (only one, Auditor Epilogue absorbs second)  \n\n**Pattern**: Early/mid, mid/late, early/late, very early/very late, late only\n\n**Principle**: Never place interludes at same chapter positions across consecutive novellas.\n\n---\n\n## BUILD-UP VS. BREAK-DOWN\n\nEach interlude uses either **build-up** (pre-crisis setup) or **break-down** (post-crisis consequences), never both in same novella.\n\n### Build-Up Methodology\n**Definition**: A-plot events before interlude setup what interlude reveals.\n\n**Example**:\n- **A-plot (Ch.4)**: Jhace notices dome scars, geometric patterns appearing\n- **Interlude 1A (after Ch.4)**: Xilcore's perspective — obsessive geometric \"corrections\"\n- **Effect**: Reader understands what Jhace witnessed\n\n**Usage**: When god-vessel activity is mysterious, interlude explains\n\n---\n\n### Break-Down Methodology\n**Definition**: Interlude explains what A-plot characters witness after.\n\n**Example**:\n- **Interlude 2A (after Ch.11)**: Blemo's purge operations shown\n- **A-plot (Ch.12)**: Refugees (Halrick) describe fires and purges\n- **Effect**: Reader knows truth before A-plot characters do\n\n**Usage**: When god-vessel activity has consequences, interlude provides context\n\n---\n\n## INTERLUDE ROTATION ACROSS NOVELLAS\n\n### N1 (GLASS)\n- **Interlude 1A** (after Ch.3): Xilcore/Corlexi (Form) — Build-up\n- **Interlude 1B** (after Ch.3): Leesa/Salee (Wholeness) — Build-up\n- **Interlude 2A** (after Ch.11): Blemo/Mobel (Purity) — Break-down\n- **Interlude 2B** (after Ch.11): Seeri/Eries (Entropy) — Break-down\n\n### N2 (GLASS)\n- **Interlude 1A** (after Ch.4): Xilcore escalation — Build-up\n- **Interlude 2A** (after Ch.12): Blemo arrival — Break-down\n# 【5†Canon_Innocent_Master_v2_INNOCENT_ONLY.md†file-SP8HddHunYzmWuRiBGepSp】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: Canon_Innocent_Master_v2_INNOCENT_ONLY.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn3file5\nContent Snippet:\n### What Magic Is\n- Manipulation of energy patterns through intention\n- Learned through practice and trial/error\n- Different practitioners discover different patterns\n- Multiple approaches to same underlying power\n\n### Magic Costs\nEvery use of magic damages the practitioner:\n- **Tremor**: Hands shake after sustained use\n- **Vein-burn**: Visible scarring in veins/tissue\n- **Exhaustion**: Physical and mental depletion\n- **Hollowing**: Terminal burnout (death of magical connection)\n\nThese costs are permanent and cumulative.\n\n### Magic Patterns Discovered (Innocent Frame)\nDifferent practitioners are discovering different ways to wield Soulpulse:\n- **Form Pattern**: Geometric precision, structural focus (Tiffani's method)\n- **Wholeness Pattern**: Integration, connection, healing\n- **Purity Pattern**: Separation, division, cleansing\n- **Entropy Pattern**: Dissolution, acceptance, change\n\nNo one fully understands the system. Practitioners figure it out through use.\n\n---\n\n## GODS AND VESSELS\n\n### God-Like Beings (Innocent Understanding)\nSome practitioners are discovering power far beyond normal mages. They're called \"god-vessels\" or simply \"gods\" by followers.\n\nFour major beings have emerged:\n- **Xilcore** (Form-perfection philosophy)\n- **Leesa** (Wholeness-healing philosophy)\n- **Blemo** (Purity-cleansing philosophy)\n- **Seeri** (Entropy-acceptance philosophy)\n\n### What They Are (Innocent Frame)\nThey appear to be:\n- Exceptionally powerful magic users\n- Capable of wielding power at unprecedented levels\n- Organizing followers around their philosophies\n- Creating ideological territories\n- Potentially divine entities (uncertain)\n\nNo character knows for certain what they are. They might be gods. They might be extraordinary humans. The truth is mysterious.\n\n---\n\n## CHARACTERS: JHACE & TIFFANI\n\n### Jhace Torrins\n**Status**: Repair technician → Magic practitioner → Powerful mage\n\nStarted as competent infrastructure worker. Discovered magical power during emergency response after the Piercing. Learned to wield Soulpulse through trial and error.\n\nBy N5, he has:\n- Mastered multiple magical patterns\n- Suffered visible costs (tremor, vein-burn)\n- Experienced profound loss (Tiffani's death)\n- Triggered massive destructive event (Fathombreak)\n- Been transformed into something beyond normal humanity\n\n### Tiffani Merrow\n**Status**: Mysterious skilled practitioner → Teacher → Sacrifice\n\nAppears in Grindheim immediately after the Piercing. Already skilled in magic despite it being newly awakened. Mysteriously competent.\n\nShe:\n- Teaches Jhace everything she knows\n- Carries trauma about someone named Senna (died years ago)\n- Will not explain her past or training\n- Loves Jhace genuinely and absolutely\n- Dies protecting him (N5)\n\nHer background is genuinely mysterious to all characters. No one knows where she came from or how she already knew magic. This remains unexplained through all 30 novellas.\n\n---\n\n## SOCIETY: ADAPTATION & ORGANIZATION\n\n### Immediate Response (N1-N5)\n- Emergency infrastructure repair\n- Population stabilization\n- Survivor trauma management\n- Civic authority collapse in some areas\n- Magic practitioners becoming alternative leaders\n\n### God-Vessel Ideology Formation (N5+)\nFour competing philosophies emerge:\n- Form-perfect order\n- Wholeness-integrated healing\n- Purity-separated cleansing\n- Entropy-accepted dissolution\n\nPeople are drawn to whichever philosophy makes most sense to them.\n\n### Conflict Potential\nDifferent ideologies will inevitably clash. By N5, this conflict is beginning to manifest.\n\n---\n# 【6†Soulpulse_Core_v2.md†file-VrwZp7vBqwt2FAMkZmeg4c】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: Soulpulse_Core_v2.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn3file6\nContent Snippet:\n**Example manifestation:**\n- Healing chronic poison by accepting the poison will remain but integrating around it\n- Mending shattered bone by accepting it will never be perfect but will function\n- Saving someone from Hollowing by accepting they'll never regain full capacity but can survive\n\n**Cost asymmetry:**\n- Both Wholeness and Entropy costs incurred simultaneously\n- Right hand suffers more damage than left (dominance asymmetry; unclear why)\n- Dual-wielding cost = ~1.5x single-principle cost per use\n\n**Danger escalation:**\n- Each dual-wielding use pushes him closer to fivefold-principle paradox capacity\n- Fivefold paradox (wielding all four simultaneously) = Fathombreak trigger (see N5 ending)\n\n### Writer Constraint: Dual-Principle Usage\n\n**Jhace can dual-wield, but:**\n\n✅ **Allowed in story:**\n- N1: First accidental dual-wield (stabilizing child)\n- N2–N4: Learning controlled dual-wield (costs become visible)\n- N4: Extreme dual-wield (Hollowing scene; Tiffani saves him)\n- N5: Fathombreak (all four principles simultaneously; one-time apocalyptic event)\n\n❌ **NOT allowed in story:**\n- Any casual dual-wielding (it should feel dangerous, rare, last-resort)\n- Any other character attempting dual-wield (only Jhace has capacity)\n- Any suggestion that dual-wield can be taught (it cannot; Jhace is unique)\n\n---\n\n## 7. HOLLOWING: TERMINAL FAILURE STATE\n\n### Definition\n\n**Hollowing** is the catastrophic burnout of vein-response capacity; channels shred from overextension; user enters shutdown state.\n\n**Outcome:** Death, permanent incapacity, or rare recovery with reduced capacity.\n\n### Triggering Conditions\n\n**Hollowing occurs when:**\n\n1. User holds Form-lock for >1 hour continuously (veins locked beyond sustainable duration)\n2. User attempts multiple catastrophic Wholeness-healings in rapid succession (veins overstimulated)\n3. User triggers Purity cascade (uncontrolled erasure spreads through vein-network)\n4. User attempts fivefold-principle paradox without preparation (channels overloaded beyond safe limit)\n5. User sustains Entropy too long (channels fully accept degradation; stops responding to reversal)\n\n### Manifestation Timeline\n\n**Phase 1: Cascade Initiation (Minutes)**\n- Intense nosebleeds (blood pressure spikes in vein-network)\n- Hallucinations (vein-stimulation affects sensory processing)\n- Confusion/disorientation (neurological disruption)\n- User often loses consciousness\n\n**Phase 2: Channel Shutdown (Hours–Days)**\n- Complete loss of vein-sensitivity (even strong conviction cannot activate veins)\n- Catatonia (user unresponsive; appears dead)\n- Body becomes fragile (user cannot move; any physical stress causes injury)\n- User cannot eat/drink (swallowing reflex fails)\n- Potential death from physical collapse\n\n**Phase 3: Possible Recovery (Days–Weeks)**\n- If user survives Phase 2, gradual sensory recovery begins\n- Vein-sensitivity returns partially (may never fully return)\n- Physical rehabilitation needed (muscles weakened; movement must be relearned)\n- Psychological trauma (memory fragmented; user may not remember Hollowing event)\n\n**Post-Hollowing Consequences:**\n- Reduced vein-sensitivity (~50% of pre-Hollowing baseline typically)\n- Permanent tremor worsening (Hollowing accelerates hand loss by ~5–10%)\n- Fear of using Soulpulse (psychological barrier; user hesitates to attempt magic)\n- Possible permanent capacity loss (rare; if veins don't recover, user cannot use Soulpulse at all)\n\n### Treatment (If Possible)\n# 【7†Canon_Innocent_Master_v2_INNOCENT_ONLY.md†file-SP8HddHunYzmWuRiBGepSp】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: Canon_Innocent_Master_v2_INNOCENT_ONLY.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn3file7\nContent Snippet:\n# Canon_Innocent_Master_v2 - INNOCENT FRAME ONLY\n\n**Document Version**: 2.1 (INNOCENCE FILTERED)\n**Created**: November 5, 2025\n**Authority**: Immutable innocent-frame canon ONLY\n**Scope**: Public truth—what readers see, what characters know, what Writers generate\n**Status**: LOCKED—for prose engine use only\n\n---\n\n## WHAT THIS CANON IS\n\nThe truth of the OmniMeta Saga world as characters experience it. veins become inert even to strong conviction\n- Symptoms: Nosebleeds, hallucinations, catatonia, potential death\n- Recovery: Uncertain; capacity may be permanently lost even if user survives\n\n**How it develops:**\n- Occurs when user pushes Soulpulse beyond sustainable limits\n- Triggers: Holding Form for >1 hour continuously; attempting to heal multiple catastrophic wounds in succession; Purity cascades; attempting fivefold principle paradox without preparation\n\n**Manifestation:**\n- Phase 1 (hours): Intense nosebleeds, hallucinations, confusion\n- Phase 2 (hours–days): Complete shutdown; user enters catatonia; veins fully inert\n- Phase 3 (days–weeks): Recovery possible but vein-sensitivity may be permanently reduced or gone\n\n**Example:** Jhace's N4 Hollowing (detailed in Dossier_Jhace.md; triggered by obsessive overwork after Bram's death)\n\n### Cost Table: By Principle\n\n| Principle | Primary Cost | Secondary Cost | Tertiary Cost | Hollowing Risk | Chronic Point |\n|-----------|--------------|-----------------|---------------|---|---|\n| **Form** | Precision tremor | Frozen hands | Rigid joints | High (overuse) | ~200 uses |\n| **Wholeness** | Fine tremor | Chronic thirst | Emotional weight | Moderate (dual-principle) | ~200 uses |\n| **Purity** | Addiction drive | Personality degradation | Nerve death (hands/feet) | VERY HIGH (cascade) | ~80 uses |\n| **Entropy** | Depression | Motivation loss | Paralysis/catatonia | Low (unless sustained) | ~250 uses |\n\n---\n\n## 6. DUAL-PRINCIPLE PARADOX: JHACE'S IMPOSSIBLE CAPACITY\n\n### Why Dual-Wielding Should Kill\n\n**Contradictory principles oppose each other at vein-level:**\n\n- Form = lock veins; Wholeness = release veins (contradiction)\n- Purity = erase; Entropy = accept decay (contradiction)\n- Any two-principle combination creates **resonance collision** in vein-substrate\n\n**Normal outcome of collision:** Veins shred; channels rupture; user dies instantly.\n\n### Why Jhace Survives\n\n**Innocent-frame explanation:** Unknown survivor's luck; rare aptitude; something about his biology\n\n**Guilty-frame explanation:** Tiffani's deliberate training; he was chosen/designed for this capacity\n\n### Jhace's Specific Paradox: Wholeness + Entropy Hybrid\n# 【11†Soulpulse_Core_v2.md†file-VrwZp7vBqwt2FAMkZmeg4c】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: Soulpulse_Core_v2.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn3file11\nContent Snippet:\n---\n\n## 8. LEARNING BY TRIAL AND ERROR: MECHANICS\n\n### How Soulpulse Is Discovered (Post-Piercing)\n\n**No instruction manual exists.** Magic must be learned through:\n\n1. **Accident:** Character attempts something instinctively; vein responds or rejects\n2. **Consequence:** Character experiences result (success or failure or injury)\n3. **Adaptation:** Character adjusts approach based on feedback\n4. **Skill:** Repeated successful attempts build mastery (and accumulate cost)\n5. **Teaching:** Rare; only experienced practitioners can teach (but teaching is imperfect; trial-and-error still dominant)\n\n### Learning Curve: Expected Timeline\n\n**First successful manipulation (any principle):** Turn 1–3 (days to weeks after Piercing)\n- Usually accidental (desperation-driven)\n- Character surprised it works\n- Cost incurred but not understood yet\n\n**Intentional single-principle use:** Turn 4–20 (weeks; trial-and-error dominates)\n- Character attempts same principle repeatedly\n- Learns to sense when it's working\n- Learns cost consequences (tremor, thirst, pain)\n- ~30 successful uses needed before reliable control\n\n**Mastery of single principle:** Turns 21–40 (months; repeated careful experimentation)\n- Character can activate principle reliably in low-stress situations\n- Can maintain stable effect for ~15 minutes without intense difficulty\n- Understands cost progression intimately\n- Still makes mistakes under pressure\n\n**Competent practitioner status:** Turns 41–80 (months to seasons; heavy use)\n- Character can activate principle in crisis (high-stress situations)\n- Can integrate multiple principle-applications in sequence\n- Understands personal limits (knows when to stop using)\n- Cost accumulation becomes visible (chronic tremor, vein-burn, etc.)\n\n**Master status:** Turns 100+ (seasons to years; intensive use)\n- Character can teach others (though teaching is imperfect)\n- Can activate principle in extreme situations\n- Has learned personal mastery limits (when to refuse requests)\n- May have attempted dual-principle or reached near-Hollowing\n\n### Trial-and-Error Failure Modes\n\n**Failure type 1: Incomplete activation**\n- User tries to activate vein but loses conviction mid-process\n- Result: Vein responds partially; creates unstable state; can cause injury\n- Example: Attempting Wholeness to heal wound but losing confidence halfway—vein half-heals; new infection develops\n\n**Failure type 2: Backlash**\n- User loses grounding/certainty while Soulpulse is active\n- Result: Vein responds opposite to intention; causes harm instead of benefit\n- Example: Attempting Form-lock but panicking during lock—structure locks wrong; snaps explosively instead\n\n**Failure type 3: Cost miscalculation**\n- User underestimates cost and pushes too hard\n- Result: Tremor/nosebleeds/pain worse than expected; user incapacitated\n- Example: Holding Form-lock for too long thinking they can sustain it—Hollowing cascade begins\n\n**Failure type 4: Principle confusion**\n- User activates wrong principle (attempts Wholeness but Purity activates)\n- Result: Unintended effect; can cause catastrophic damage\n- Example: Attempting to heal poisoned person using Wholeness but Purity activates instead—poison erased but person harmed in process\n\n### Writer-Facing Rule: Trial and Error\n\n**Every first or experimental use of Soulpulse must show:**\n- Uncertainty (character unsure if it will work)\n- Consequence (positive, negative, or mixed result)\n- Learning (character adjusts understanding based on outcome)\n- Cost (visible toll incurred)\n\n**Cannot skip through learning process.** Each new technique/principle requires scene-time showing trial-and-error discovery.\n\n---\n# 【12†Dossier_Jhace_Torrins_Innocent.md†file-RE6Pf7PjNrRFKnj5Jiq3R3】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: Dossier_Jhace_Torrins_Innocent.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn3file12\nContent Snippet:\n**Learning Curve** (N1–N2):\n- Accidental successes teach him vein-sensing\n- Tiffani guides him toward intentional Wholeness work\n- Costs appear immediately: tremor, thirst, exhaustion\n- By N2, he can stabilize infrastructure (heat pipes, domes) and heal minor injuries\n\n**Mastery Progression**:\n- **N1–N2**: Accidental healing; Mass casualties. Gods fully manifest in mortal vessels.\n\n**Cost**: Jhace survives but is fundamentally changed. Hand function improves (48% right, 28% left) but new capacity comes with hidden cost (revealed in later novellas).\n\n### Confluence State (N6–N30)\n\n**Definition**: Dual-wielding contradictory principles without dying. Jhace is the first Confluence practitioner.\n# 【13†01_Progression_Timeline_Master_INNOCENT_ONLY.md†file-KvRepn8rVmKGRHUh71MRFc】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: Soulpulse_Core_v2.md\n\n**Document Version**: 2.0  \n**Created**: October 30, 2025 (23:20 CDT)  \n**Authority**: Immutable hard magic rules  \n**Scope**: Vein substrate, four principles, access requirements, cost architecture, learning mechanics  \n**Status**: LOCKED—all magic scenes anchor here; no exceptions or deviations  \n\n**Related Files**:\n- `Canon_Innocent_Master_v2_CORRECTED.md` — Innocent-frame context, Piercing activation\n- `Lexicon_Temporal_TeOga.md` — Time references (Tide/Anneal/Crucible/Casting)\n- `Dossier_Jhace.md` — Hand damage progression (hard mechanical limits)\n- `Dossier_Tiffani_Auditor_CounterSpark.md` — Vein-burn progression (hard mechanical limits)\n\n---\n\n## TABLE OF CONTENTS\n\n1. Vein Substrate: The Invisible Stress Architecture\n2. What Soulpulse Is (Hard Definition)\n3. Access Requirement: Conviction\n4. The Four Principles (Hard Mechanics)\n5. Cost Architecture: What Magic Demands\n6. Dual-Principle Paradox: Jhace's Impossible Capacity\n7. Hollowing: Terminal Failure State\n8. Learning by Trial and Error: Mechanics\n9. Forbidden Language (Prose Law Integration)\n\n---\n\n## 1. VEIN SUBSTRATE: THE INVISIBLE STRESS ARCHITECTURE\n\n### What Are Veins?\n\n**Veins** are invisible channels of structural stress that exist within all materials (objects, living tissue, the planetary substrate itself).\n\n**Pre-Piercing state:** Veins exist but are **inert**—stress channels locked in place, unresponsive to will or intention.\n\n**Post-Piercing state:** The projectile's alien materials cause **vein-infection**—veins throughout Te'Oga become **responsive to conviction and Soulpulse manipulation**.\n\n### Vein States: Three Conditions\n\nEvery vein exists in one of three states:\n\n#### 1. Stable\n\n**Definition:** Veins in equilibrium; stress distributed normally; material/body functioning as intended.\n\n**Indicators:** No sensations; object holds; body healthy; no tremor or pain.\n\n**Manipulation:** Stable veins are difficult to deliberately activate; require high conviction and precise application.\n\n**Narrative use:** Characters describe stable objects as \"holding\" or \"settled\"; bodies feel \"intact\" or \"whole\".\n\n#### 2. Stressed\n\n**Definition:** Veins under unusual pressure; stress accumulating; material/body approaching failure point.\n\n**Indicators:** Humming sensation; pressure-feeling (like water-weight); localized pain; tremor in proximate tissue.\n\n**Manipulation:** Stressed veins are easiest to manipulate; they respond to conviction quickly; cost is moderate.\n\n**Narrative use:** Characters describe stressed objects as \"creaking\" or \"singing\" (forbidden: \"humming like a tuning fork\"); bodies feel \"stretched\" or \"tight\".\n\n#### 3. Rupturing\n\n**Definition:** Veins in cascading failure; stress exceeding maximum threshold; material/body approaching structural collapse.\n\n**Indicators:** Intense pain; visible cracks appearing; explosive sensation (pressure-release imminent); nosebleeds if in living tissue.\n\n**Manipulation:** Rupturing veins cannot be stabilized through normal Soulpulse (cost too high; would kill user); can only be managed through Wholeness-braiding (accepting the failure and integrating around it) or accelerated through Entropy (allowing graceful collapse).\n\n**Narrative use:** Characters describe rupturing objects as \"screaming\" (forbidden: \"singing like a broken instrument\"); bodies feel \"shattering\" or \"dissolving from inside\".\n# 【15†Soulpulse_Core_v2.md†file-VrwZp7vBqwt2FAMkZmeg4c】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: Soulpulse_Core_v2.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn3file15\nContent Snippet:\n**Narrative use:** Characters describe rupturing objects as \"screaming\" (forbidden: \"singing like a broken instrument\"); bodies feel \"shattering\" or \"dissolving from inside\".\n\n### Vein Density: Geographic Distribution\n\nVein density (responsive veins per cubic meter) varies by location post-Piercing:\n\n| Location | Vein Density | Responsiveness | Cost Modifier |\n|----------|--------------|-----------------|---------------|\n| Grindheim (Underface, near entry) | 95%+ | Extreme (veins respond instantly) | x1.5 cost (veins too sensitive) |\n| Mid-Underface cities | 70–80% | High (veins respond reliably) | x1.0 cost (baseline) |\n| Underface periphery | 40–50% | Moderate (veins respond inconsistently) | x0.8 cost (easier manipulation) |\n| Curtain zone | Fluctuates wildly | Chaotic (veins respond unpredictably) | x2.0+ cost (dangerous) |\n| Outer Crown entry | 60–70% | High (veins respond reliably) | x1.0 cost (baseline) |\n| Mid-Outer Crown | 30–50% | Moderate (veins respond inconsistently) | x0.8 cost (easier manipulation) |\n| Outer Crown periphery | 10–20% | Low (veins barely respond) | x0.5 cost (very difficult to activate) |\n\n**Narrative consequence:** Magic is hardest (costliest) in Grindheim; easiest in periphery; fluctuates unpredictably in Curtain zone.\n\n---\n\n## 2. WHAT SOULPULSE IS (HARD DEFINITION)\n\n### Core Mechanism\n\n**Soulpulse** is the deliberate manipulation of vein state through focused conviction and directed internal energy.\n\n**Process:**\n1. User senses vein(s) in a material or living tissue\n2. User focuses conviction on specific vein target\n3. User channels internal energy (metabolic, emotional, or both) into the target vein\n4. Vein responds by shifting state (stable → stressed, stressed → rupturing, or reversed)\n5. Material/body responds to vein state change (object strengthens/weakens; wound heals/tears; structure adjusts)\n\n### Prerequisites for Successful Soulpulse\n\n**User must possess:**\n\n1. **Vein sensitivity** — ability to sense veins within materials/bodies\n   - Post-Piercing baseline: 70% of population develops some sensitivity\n   - Trainable: with practice, sensitivity increases\n   - Genetic component: some people naturally gifted; others require years of practice\n\n2. **Conviction** — psychological state of absolute certainty + grounding + acceptance of cost\n   - **Certainty:** User must know exactly what they intend to accomplish (vague intentions fail)\n   - **Grounding:** User must be emotionally anchored (panic/fear causes manipulation to fail)\n   - **Cost acceptance:** User must consciously accept the physical toll (hesitation causes incomplete manipulation or backlash)\n\n3. **Energy reserves** — metabolic and emotional capacity to fuel the manipulation\n   - Soulpulse draws on internal energy (blood sugar, emotional intensity, willpower)\n   - Depletion causes fatigue, tremor, nosebleeds\n   - Different principles draw on different energy types (Form = willpower; Wholeness = emotional; Purity = rage; Entropy = acceptance)\n\n### What Soulpulse CANNOT Do\n# 【16†Soulpulse_Core_v2.md†file-VrwZp7vBqwt2FAMkZmeg4c】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: Soulpulse_Core_v2.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn3file16\nContent Snippet:\n---\n\n## 4. THE FOUR PRINCIPLES (HARD MECHANICS)\n\n### Principle 1: Form (Corlexi Tradition) — God-Vessel: Xilcore\n\n**What Form does:** Locks veins into geometric precision; structures become perfectly stable within defined patterns.\n\n**Activation mechanism:**\n- User visualizes precise geometric pattern (shape, angle, measurement)\n- User channels willpower (not emotion; requires cold clarity)\n- Veins in target material respond by locking into pattern-alignment\n- Result: Structure held in perfect stability for duration of concentration\n\n**Duration:** Lasts as long as user maintains concentration (breaks if user distracted, injured, or concentration lapses)\n\n**Cost per use:**\n- **Primary:** Precision fatigue (fine motor tremor develops; worsens with repeated use)\n- **Secondary:** Frozen hands (loss of sensation in fingertips; can become permanent if overused)\n- **Tertiary:** Rigidity (user's own joints become stiff; chronic tension develops)\n\n**Failure mode:** If user loses concentration while Form-locked, locked structure **snaps back violently**; sudden release of stress energy can cause explosive failure.\n\n**Narrative markers (innocent-frame):**\n- User reports feeling \"crystal-clear\" mentally but \"locked\" in body\n- Structures described as \"perfect\" or \"precise\" or \"geometrically locked\"\n- After use: tremor visible in hands; user reports finger numbness\n\n#### Form-Advanced Technique: Dual-Principle Form-Lock\n\n(Tiffani's signature technique; taught to Jhace in N4 Hollowing scene)\n\n**What it does:** Combines Form-locking with Wholeness-braiding to lock internal veins while simultaneously stabilizing around failure points.\n\n**Activation:** Requires wielding both Form and Wholeness simultaneously (normally impossible; Jhace's paradox capacity allows this in N4)\n\n**Effect:** Can stabilize rupturing veins without full healing; maintains function while damaged tissue remains.\n\n**Cost:** Extreme (both Form and Wholeness costs incurred simultaneously; accelerates Hollowing risk)\n\n**Example:** Tiffani using Form to lock Jhace's degraded vein architecture in place while Wholeness-braiding integrates around the damage—keeping him functioning despite Hollowing state.\n\n---\n\n### Principle 2: Wholeness (Salee Tradition) — God-Vessel: Leesa\n\n**What Wholeness does:** Integrates damaged veins together; wounds heal; broken systems mend; living tissue restores.\n\n**Activation mechanism:**\n- User focuses emotional conviction on damaged area\n- User channels compassion/love/acceptance into target veins\n- Veins respond by bridging damaged sections; living tissue integrates around breaks\n- Result: Wound heals; function restores (imperfectly; scars remain but tissue is viable)\n\n**Duration:** Permanent (healing integrates vein-bridges into new tissue structure; doesn't fade)\n\n**Cost per use:**\n- **Primary:** Tremor (nerve endings stimulated by vein-integration; tremor develops or worsens)\n- **Secondary:** Thirst (metabolic exhaustion from healing energy expenditure; requires huge water/food intake)\n- **Tertiary:** Emotional weight (user absorbs sensation of pain being healed; experiences phantom aching)\n\n**Failure mode:** If user loses emotional grounding while Wholeness is active, integrated veins **rupture from incomplete bridging**; creates new wound worse than original.\n\n**Narrative markers (innocent-frame):**\n- User reports feeling \"connected\" to injured person; experiences their pain\n- Wounds described as \"knitting together\" or \"integrating\" or \"healing wrong but holding\"\n- After use: tremor obvious; user extremely thirsty; emotional exhaustion visible\n# 【17†03_Character_Arc_Tracker_INNOCENT_ONLY.md†file-4KDXgBk9oTNnC424MYNFL3】\nContent source: Source.file\nTitle: 03_Character_Arc_Tracker_INNOCENT_ONLY.md\nCitation Marker: fileciteturn3file17\nContent Snippet:\n# CHARACTER ARC TRACKER (INNOCENT ONLY)\n\n**Document Version**: 2.1 (INNOCENCE FILTERED)\n**Scope**: Character development as genuinely experienced\n**Status**: For prose engine use only\n\n---\n\n## JHACE TORRINS: TRANSFORMATION THROUGH CRISIS\n\n### N1-N5 Arc\n- **Start**: Competent technician, isolated, predictable life\n- **Crisis 1 (N1 Ch.3)**: Piercing, discovers magic instinctively\n- **Development**: Learning magic, deepening with Tiffani\n- **Crisis 2 (N3)**: Bram's death, grief spiral begins\n- **Crisis 3 (N4)**: Hollowing, near-death experience\n- **Transformation**: Four-pattern capability, grief-forged power\n- **End (N5)**: Alone, powerful, grieving absolutely\n\n### N6-N10 Arc\n- Mastery of unprecedented power\n- Grief processing\n- Leading survivors\n- Resistance to god-vessels forming\n- Deepening relationships with crew\n\n### Overall Arc (N1-N30)\nJhace becomes the anchor point for surviving god-war.
