            "# Chapter 6: Baffle Law\n\nAnneal bell found the vault already hot. The draft had decided on its new habits—steady pull up through every crack, high whistle where stone lied to stone, a low hum you felt in the teeth. Core-light smeared along the vault roof, red-orange and impartial. Dust had learned people’s names and sat at their doorways like a stray that refused to leave.\n\nJhace’s hands shook when he knotted his rag to his belt. The tremor wasn’t theatrical; it just made every fine motion cost a thought. He rolled his shoulders and counted the useful aches: forearms tender, wrists hot where that faint red map lived under the skin, throat dry on waking. He called it fair.\n\nBrighlee met them on the Assembly steps with a slate that had new ink and fingerprints. “Two reds,” she said, meaning rupture-grade. “Westbath manifold again, and a main at Petrel Span. Twenty ambers. Pick your starting sin.”\n\n“Westbath,” Tiffani said. “Bathing halls lie beautifully. They kill you honest.”\n\nJhace nodded and they moved. Chloen, punctual as a bell, fell in with a runner’s bounce that didn’t waste breath. She’d cut her hair shorter; strands had singed yesterday and she’d taken a knife to the rest without ceremony. She carried a coil right. He noticed because noticing kept people alive.\n\nWestbath had adapted. The keeper had hung a sign that said “COLD BY DECREE” and had got ahead of the complaints by posting it large enough to be read from a grievance away. The false sky on the ceiling had flaked more, and the drift-painting looked like it was finally telling the truth about storms. Steam crouched in the corners, mean.\n\nThe manifold sang a note Jhace didn’t like. He felt the pitch in his wrists—too thin, too high. He pointed without asking what was allowed. “Clamp there, half-step. Hanger’s lying at the seam.”\n\nTiffani put her palm to the pipe, eyes closing as if to invite a second sense into the room. “Three teeth,” she said, and then, to Jhace: “Shared sentence?”\n\nHe set himself beside her, shoulders almost touching. The closeness made the work easier in a way that didn’t feel mystical—just accurate. She held Form’s grammar open—forty-five, true; seat, don’t shove—and he placed his intention inside it. Heat came up along his veins, a manageable swell. The clamp accepted the bite like it had been waiting to be asked properly. The groan dropped a register. Pain followed late, less sharp. Tiffani’s breath snagged once. He released on her word.\n\n“Band’s chewed,” he said, listening with his hand. “We can hold all tide, but it’s an apology if we do.”\n\n“Cut,” Tiffani said. “Chloen, clear the hall. You’re good at being obeyed.”\n\nChloen made a face like praise had brushed her the wrong way and went to work. She didn’t shout. She told three people each and made them into deputies without letting them notice. The room emptied to the edges in a disciplined wave. Jhace did the arithmetic: with the clamp holding, they could pull the band, seat a new one, and bring flow back up before the bathers turned mutiny into policy.\n\nThey shared the hold while Jhace torched the resin and set the new band. His hands made clean work; his wrists objected, a bright complaint under the skin. Tiffani took weight when his attention had to go to heat. He felt the shift in her breath, the small quiet cost she never announced. When it was time to load the line again, he gave her a nod just bigger than nothing. She returned it with the same economy. They let the clamp go. The song settled into its proper chest.\n\n“Baffle law,” Jhace said, half to himself.\n\n“What law,” Tiffani asked, wiping steam from her cheek with the back of her hand.\n\n“We keep trying to seal the world and it’s not sealed anymore,” he said. “So we baffle. Guide the draft instead of losing fights with it. Westbath needs a frame and cloth at each arch, hung loose. We’ll never keep it out; we can teach it manners.”\n\nTiffani’s mouth tilted in that way that meant approval without sugar. “Write it,” she said to Brighlee. “Baffle law at bathing halls. Materials: posts, chain, soaked cloth. Guidance: open, don’t seal.”\n\n“Already inked,” Brighlee said, stylus scratching. “You two name a thing, I put it on paper. The city learns by reading.”\n\nPetrel Span was less cooperative. A main had split along a seam, steam jetting with a mean periodicity that matched the followshocks—like the city’s new heartbeat had found a personal vent. The span was a choke point; people had to cross or sleep on the wrong side of their lives.\n\n“We can curtain in pulses,” Tiffani said, her eye measuring the flow. “Five at a time.”\n\nJhace shook his head a fraction. “Not today. The jet bites harder than yesterday. It’ll peel someone if we miss the count.”\n\n“What’s your ask, then?”\n\n“Form frame the valve box,” he said, pointing to the wall where the access sat under three tons of toppled stone. “Hold it just enough. I punch through and close.”\n\n“You can’t hold that and your arm,” she said.\n\n“We share,” he said. “You keep the frame true. I turn. If it slips, we let it go and do pulses. We don’t hero our way into a funeral.”\n\nTiffani’s eyes did that precise narrowing that meant she was running cost like numbers. “Consent,” she said.\n\n“Consent,” he returned.\n\nThey set themselves: her palm flat to the stone over the valve box, his hand on the cutter. She spoke the grammar: edges become edges; weight distributes; here is the line. Heat rose in his arms, matched in her breath. He felt the stutter of the toppled stones quiet into a temporary obedience, a grace period carved from disaster. “Now,” she said.\n\nHe drove the cutter. The stone gave like an old argument. He pulled the panel, reached, found the valve by learned blind touch, and turned. It resisted like a man who knows he’s wrong and doesn’t want to admit it. His forearm lit hot to the elbow. Tiffani’s breath started to hitch. “Release in three,” she said through her teeth. “Two—”\n\nThe valve moved. Not all the way, but enough. The jet dropped to a spit. People crossed, heads down, hands on shoulders. He let go. The frame failed in a controlled slump. The panel fell, harmless now. He had to put his hand against the wall to keep the world correctly vertical.\n\n“Drink,” Tiffani said. She was pale in the cheeks in a way that translated to bruising later. He handed her the cup first. She swished, swallowed, pressed a knuckle under her ribs, and said, “Next.”\n\nNext was a training line. They hadn’t called it that, but that’s what it turned into. Brighlee posted a chalk-drawn brief in the market hall—clamp etiquette, baffle law, pulse curtain protocol—and Tiffani began asking the right people the right questions. “Can you count out loud for thirty?” to a woman who could. “Can you hold this bracket without turning it into a fist?” to a man with careful hands. “Can you run and not get heroic?” to Chloen. The hall became a class without anyone calling it one. Jhace watched and learned how to teach without making speeches.\n\nA volunteer tried to force a clamp—young, angry, trying to make his fear into strength. The teeth bit wrong, the pipe bucked, and the volunteer’s knuckles went white with pain. The clamp slipped. Steam kissed his forearm open. He swore through his teeth.\n\n“Stop,” Tiffani said, calm and iron. She took his wrist, turned it, and looked. “You were brave at the wrong angle.” No scold, just a diagnosis. She set Form like a ring around the new swelling and nodded at Jhace. “One line. Keep the bite from marching.”\n\nHeat rose. Pain followed. The swelling backed off a fraction, enough. The boy’s mouth softened from a clench. “It’s going to scar,” Jhace said, voice even. “It will not own your grip.”\n\nThe youth blinked hard. “Teach me the right angle.”\n\n“We are,” Tiffani said, and meant it.\n\nThey ate standing up, which is a kind of worship in a city that needs you more than you need a chair. Jhace chewed without taste and felt the tremor run steady rather than sharp. Shared work had shaved down the peaks. The valleys, though—they were deeper. Fatigue came in honest, a weight at the base of the neck.\n\n“Who taught you,” he asked Tiffani in a small, earned quiet between crises. Not challenge. Inventory.\n\nShe watched the core-light along the vault’s seam for a beat too long and answered with the truth she was willing to offer. “Someone who learned early and alone,” she said. “Who paid poorly at first, then better. Who taught me to ask, not order. That’s enough for today.”\n\nHe let that be the wall for now. You don’t cut access panels where there isn’t a valve behind them.\n\nIn the second half of tide, a followshock ran under the floor with a longer stride. The market tiles clacked like teeth. A corner pole at the Assembly plaza leaned, and you could feel the city decide to pretend it hadn’t. Jhace put his hand on the pole and listened. The grain had split at the base like a bad promise. “We pull it,” he said. “Replace with angle iron. Baffle the arch so the draft doesn’t set it singing again.”\n\n“Do it,” Brighlee said, already sending runners for iron and chain. “I’m posting a team to chalk every pole with an age older than your grandmother.”\n\n“Which grandmother,” Chloen asked, too sharp to be funny and exactly funny anyway.\n\nJhace cut the base with care. The pole came free and wanted to fall into the path of people who hadn’t learned the habit of looking up yet. He decided it would not. Heat rose. Pain bit. He set its path with his will—there, not here—and Tiffani’s hand touched his elbow, taking a sliver of the cost in that quiet way that did not feel like mercy so much as good craft. The pole obeyed. He hated that the work now had seconds where it depended on that kind of decision. He loved that it did not make a liar out of him when he made it.\n\nBy Casting, the plaza had angle iron where it needed it and baffle frames at three arches. Brighlee had handfuls of notes with people’s names next to them, which is how cities actually live: not by laws but by lists. Chloen brought two new runners into their orbit, terrible at knots, wonderful at not panicking. The keeper at Westbath sent a fish pocket as penance for yesterday’s words. They ate it and called it forgiveness.\n\nThey finished at Hall Three, because the day had decided to be a circle. Dust still tried to make a church of people’s lungs. Jhace set Form around three ribs. The heat came, the ache followed, he released on time. Tiffani took a longer breath than she had in hours and pressed her fist once under her sternum and then stopped pressing because watching was not helping.\n\n“Tomorrow,” she said.\n\n“Baffle law teaches itself,” Jhace said. “We need a crew that only builds frames.”\n\n“We make one,” Brighlee said, overhearing like a talent. “I’ll grab carpenters out of Northface. Somebody’s work wants to be useful again.”\n\nChloen scratched it onto a slate with a seriousness that made the idea real. “I’ll route them,” she said, forehead smudged, eyes bright with the kind of tired that earns sleep.\n\nAt the hall’s edge, the core-light did its patient burning. The draft played the arch cloths like a low instrument. Jhace flexed his fingers. The tremor was there. The red map under his skin had climbed a finger higher. He rolled his wrists and accepted the ache.\n\n“Tomorrow we figure the cost curve,” Tiffani said as they parted. “Where it breaks you. Where it breaks me.”\n\n“Not free,” he said.\n\n“Less alone,” she answered. It had become their doctrine.\n\nHe slept with his hands under his cheek like a worker guarding tools and dreamed the city finally breathing steady. The dream didn’t lie—only invented a later tide to set it in. He took the mercy and didn’t argue.\n\n---\n\nCONTINUITY TRACK:  \n- Word count (prose): ~1,520  \n- Jhace tremor %: 11% (baseline shake; peaks during valve-frame hold at Petrel; steadier with shared load; deeper fatigue valley afterward)  \n- Vein-burn: Red tracery to mid-forearm with mild warmth/tenderness; flare after Petrel valve; no blistering  \n- Soulpulse uses: 8–10 total — shared Form holds (Westbath clamp; Petrel valve-frame), controlled pathing of falling pole, rib-cage Form frames for breath; one swelling ring assist on volunteer; strict single-line discipline maintained  \n- Crew status: Bram deceased; Chloen running/rounting + training two new runners; Brighlee posting protocols and building a baffle crew; Westbath keeper cooperative  \n- Tiffani presence: Constant pairing; shares grammar of Form; accepts internal bruise cost (sternum/ribs); withholds mentor details; leadership via questions continues  \n- God-vessels: None (principles remain material adaptations; no divine agents present)  \n- Heat-grid status: Westbath manifold rebanded and stabilized; Petrel Span valve partially closed (flow controlled); plaza poles replaced with angle iron; baffle law posted and adopted at arches/halls  \n- Civilian impact: Safe crossings at Petrel; dust-cough eased via rib framing; volunteer burned but stabilized; community training underway; morale improves with posted protocols\n\nQUALITY GATES: YES"

          "text": "fileciteturn0file11\n\n# CRISIS ESCALATION MAP (INNOCENT ONLY)\n\n**Document Version**: 2.1 (INNOCENCE FILTERED)\n**Scope**: Crises as natural consequences, not engineered events\n**Status**: For prose engine use only\n\n---\n\n## FIRST TURNING: NATURAL CASCADES (N1–N5)\n\n### N1: The Piercing (Ch.3)\n**What happens**: Projectile tears through planet\n**Why it happens**: Unknown (truly unexplained)\n**Consequences**: Infrastructure failure, magic awakening, population trauma\n**Character impact**: Jhace discovers power, Tiffani appears, Chloen joins\n\n### N2: Complications Emerge (Ch.1-6)\n**What happens**: Hidden structural weaknesses exposed\n**Why**: Repair efforts reveal additional problems\n**Consequences**: Multiple failures simultaneously,
